Hardware: British and American Galvanized Iron Prices Rise, Sales Stagnate 157

The market for galvanized iron, regardless of British or American goods, has felt a shortage of goods since the Building Committee released a large number of spot goods. The industry, aware of this, and with financially wealthy trading houses taking the opportunity to hoard, has led to a gradual increase in spot prices. Currently, 48-gauge American goods are estimated at 15 taels 2.5 qian per dan, 38-gauge at 15 taels 7.5 qian, 33-gauge at 14 taels 7.5 qian, and 25-gauge at 13 taels 7.5 qian. British goods, 31-gauge 7-foot are estimated at 9 qian 2 fen per sheet, 6-foot at 8 qian 1 fen, 28-gauge at 11 taels 7.5 qian, 26-gauge at 11 taels 2.5 qian, and 24-gauge at 10 taels 7 qian. All standards are three fen to one tael and a half higher than before. However, customer sales have been unable to keep up recently due to the increased prices, so actual transactions have been unusually sluggish. It is found that only two or three hundred bundles have been sold in the market in the past three or four days. It is heard that exports are even more desolate. According to those familiar with this commodity, whether this commodity can stand firm after the price increase depends on how the overseas pricing will change in the future.

Coal: Japanese Coal After the Bombing 158

Since the Blood and Soul Corps bombed Yongchang Coal Company, warning the treacherous merchant Wu Jichang, most of the merchants in this port who specialize in selling Japanese coal for profit have been vigilant. The market trading yesterday was slightly restrained, and some of the more timid and those with more spot goods were willing to sell at lower prices. For example, Matsuura lump coal was sold yesterday for only 8 taels 2.5 qian per ton, Kanda lump coal for 7 taels, and Yuanchu lump coal for 5 taels. However, there were still few buyers.

Local News

Northeast National Salvation Army Command Headquarters 159

Shanghai Office Established

Affairs Temporarily Handled by Wang Zhiyuan

Since the Japanese occupation of the three northeastern provinces on September 18th, they initially sought to invade Shanghai and then coerced and enticed traitors to establish a puppet state. Zhu Jiqing, a member of the Central Committee, originally from the Northeast, disguised himself and secretly went to various parts of the three northeastern provinces several months ago. He systematically and methodically contacted local people who had spontaneously organized national salvation armies, volunteer armies, and self-defense forces, and organized the Northeast National Salvation Army Command Headquarters to facilitate long-term resistance against Japan. Zhu returned to Nanjing on the 18th of this month and immediately came to Shanghai to seek assistance from various parties and to negotiate everything. In order to facilitate contact with all parties, the headquarters specially established an office in Shanghai. All affairs of the office are temporarily handled by Wang Zhiyuan, the former propaganda director of the 19th Route Army. The office has established various departments, including an economic committee, a propaganda committee, a transportation committee, and a secretariat, and is now actively engaged in carrying out its work. The situation in all aspects is described in detail below.

Central Government's Assistance: Wang Jingwei, the President of the Executive Yuan, believes that Zhu's trip out of the customs to inspect everything in the three northeastern provinces for three months, despite the hardships and dangers, and to organize the Northeast National Salvation Army, organizing and training the scattered and undisciplined people there, deserves full assistance. His subordinate troops are divided into the First, Second, Third, and Fourth Route Armies, each route army is divided into three detachments, and each detachment has about two divisions. It is estimated that there are a total of 150,000 people in the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang.

Attitude of the 19th Army: The 19th Route Army expressed great sympathy for Zhu Jiqing's efforts to contact volunteer armies in various places and his determination to resist Japan. In addition to sending representatives to contact Zhu and reporting on the army's military plans during the Shanghai war, they also promised to provide material assistance. They were particularly impressed by the bravery of Wang Delin's volunteer army in Jilin in fighting the enemy.

Economic Committee: The Northeast National Salvation Army Command Headquarters, recognizing the lack of ammunition and pay for the volunteer armies in the three northeastern provinces, believed that no matter how hard the volunteer armies fought, if there were no adequate preparations or assistance in terms of supplies, the result would inevitably be failure. Therefore, it specially established an economic committee in Shanghai to handle all economic matters and appointed well-known figures from various places to work together to advance the effort. The committee was established on July 30th. Those present included Tang Jicang, Wu Shan, Yin Ruli, Chu Fucheng, Li Cishan, Yu Buju, Liu Houwu, Wang Zhiyuan, Guo Juru, and dozens of others. Wang Zhiyuan was publicly elected as chairman to report on the establishment of the army's Shanghai office and the fundraising situation of the economic committee. Subsequently, Chu Fucheng, Yin Ruli, Li Cishan, Yu Buju, Tang Jicang, Wu Shan, Liu Houwu, and others expressed their opinions and had considerable ideas on how to assist the volunteer armies in the Northeast.

Propaganda Committee: The members of the committee are Wang Lixi, Xia Qifeng, Zhu Pu, Zheng Jijie, Xie Bainian, Cai Youmin, Li Yiwei, Li Wude, Chen Kan, Liu Shumo, Xu Zhiyuan, Qiao Yifan, Huang Weizhong, Zhuang Zhuoying, Zheng Jingqu, Liu Xuanzui, Fu Wumen, etc. The committee decided to establish a news agency and organize a Northeast Problem Research Association, inviting people from all walks of life in Shanghai to specialize in studying the Northeast problem.

Transportation Committee: The members of the committee are Ding Zhenheng, Lu Yinquan, Chen Xinghan, Cao Jitang, Li Zhiping, Yao Tezhuo, etc. They are currently engaged in handling transportation affairs in various parts of the Northeast.

Organization and Troops: The organizational system of the Northeast National Salvation Army is led by the Commander-in-Chief, who is in charge of the entire army. Under the Commander-in-Chief, there are commanders of each route army, and then detachment leaders (below the detachment are divisions, regiments, battalions, and companies), guerrilla detachment leaders, and security detachment leaders. The detachments are responsible for frontline combat, the guerrilla detachments are responsible for disrupting enemy defenses, and the security detachments are responsible for maintaining rear security. The headquarters and the headquarters of each route army have military, political, financial, and security committees as design and advisory bodies. Each route army, each independent detachment, and each independent division are assigned a political and military special commissioner by the headquarters to represent the headquarters and be responsible for supervision and command. As of now, the established units include the First, Second, Third, and Fourth Route Armies, and Wang Delin's special route (Wang is the Eastern Route Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast National Salvation Army). Each route army has two to three detachments in its combat force, and each detachment has two or more divisions. In addition, there are two independent detachments, twelve independent divisions, and several independent cavalry regiments and training regiments that do not belong to any route army. In terms of its actual strength, the combined forces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang total 150,000 people, with about 100,000 concentrated in the Liaoning-Ning area and about 50,000 in the Jilin-Heilongjiang area. Other troops are also being contacted or organized, and they must gradually become an organization to concentrate strength and complete the common mission of saving the country. The leaders of the armed people resisting Japan in the Northeast include Liu Chunqi (Liangshan), Ma Zidan, Bao Enpu, Meng Yuhua, Yang Jiuzhou, Zhang Zuoqing, Sun Yutang, Zheng Guilin, Li Ziyang, Wang Zemin, Liu Zhendong in the Liaoxi area,

Li Haifeng, Huang Tieshan, Jin Ziming, Gao Pengzhen (Tizi), Gao Zhonghua, Zhang Guowei, Sun Yutian, Yu Mingzhong, Li Leting, Wang Zhaopan, Fan Junchen, Lao Beifeng, etc. In the Liaodong area, there are Liu Kejian, Wang Quanyi, Li Juchuan, Wang Yamin, Liu Xiangge, Zhong Zichen, Wang Ruiwu, Tang Juwu, Deng Tiemei, Li Zirong, etc. In the Jilin-Heilongjiang area, there are Wang Delin, Wei Shimin, Li Haiqing, Yu Zuosheng, Wu Fangqiu, Chen Deshun, etc. Among these people, some are local gentry, some are heads of local militias, some are leaders of bandits, and some are retired military and police officers. Most have joined the National Army and the National Salvation Army. Others who call themselves volunteer armies or self-defense forces all agree with the general headquarters' consistent stance and actions, such as destroying the Sujiatun station of the South Manchuria Railway, the Anshan Iron and Steel Works, and attacking Liaozhong County, Yixian County, Jinxi County, and Beizhen County. They can all disregard their own safety and lead the people forward. Their strong patriotism is truly admirable.

The Situation of the Chinese and Japanese Armies: The Japanese army has two major shortcomings in its operations in the Northeast: (1) The battle line is too long. The Japanese army occupies no less than five to six thousand miles of railway lines, and the area on both sides of the railway is our territory. Its battle line is more than ten thousand miles long, making it difficult to coordinate everything; (2) It cannot fight scattered battles. The Japanese army is good at joint operations of infantry, cavalry, artillery, and air force, but it has never used a single type of soldier to fight. It feels very tired of running around against our guerrilla-style scattered battles. Moreover, during the sixth, seventh, and eighth months of the lunar calendar, dense sorghum and trees are everywhere in the fields, which is tantamount to creating natural hiding places for us, which is enough to give the Japanese army a fatal blow. However, at the same time, we also have two major shortcomings: (1) Lack of ammunition. Ammunition is the most necessary thing for combat, but the ammunition used by the armed people in the Northeast is extremely scarce. If this continues, we will inevitably lose our combat effectiveness; (2) Uncoordinated command. There are about hundreds of thousands of volunteer soldiers in the Northeast. The so-called volunteer soldiers refer to the armed forces resisting Japan, which can be divided into two types: formal army and armed civilians. The troops of Ma Zhanshan, Ding Chao, Li Du, etc. belong to the former, and the National Salvation Army, the Volunteer Army, and the Self-Defense Army, etc. belong to the latter. This type of armed civilian is untrained, large in number, complex in situation, vast in area, and inconvenient in transportation. It is often difficult to achieve effective command in combat against the enemy. Regarding the second point, people of insight from all walks of life are working hard to improve it. The current situation is gradually becoming unified. Regarding the first point, it is indeed an extremely serious problem. It is hoped that the central government and compatriots at home and abroad will pay close attention to it and provide full assistance. Then the enemy will be exhausted and unable to govern peacefully. If we continue to work hard and persevere to the end, I believe that there will be a day when we will regain our sovereignty.

Enthusiastic Participation: After Zhu returned to Nanjing from the three northeastern provinces, he immediately went to Shanghai. All young and ambitious people rose up at the news and petitioned to go to the Northeast to participate in the volunteer army's operations. In order to commend the enthusiastic uprising of young people, Zhu has allowed them to be sent to the Northeast in batches. Two trains departed from Nanjing last week and one train will depart this Friday. Zhu is expected to return north next Monday, and it is said that there will be dozens of people accompanying him.

Research Association for Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan 160

Second Meeting Held Yesterday

Opinions on the Silver Content of the New Currency Remain Divided

It Was Decided to Hold a Third Meeting on the 3rd of Next Month to Discuss

According to the Central News Agency, the Research Association for Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan held its second meeting at the Central Bank at 2:30 pm yesterday and adjourned at 4:15 pm. It was decided to hold a third meeting next Wednesday. Chen Jian'an, the chairman of the association, went to Song's residence on Qiqi Road after the meeting to report the progress of the meeting to Finance Minister Song.

Committee Members Present: The committee members present at yesterday's meeting included Chen Jian'an, Bei Songsun, Liu Hongsheng, Hu Bijiang, Geng Aide, Mai Zhaote, Lei Qi, as well as Ma Jiliang, representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Hu Mengjia, representative of the Bankers' Association, Yu Zuoting, representative of the Money Dealers' Association, and Coxon (manager of Jardine Matheson), representative of the Western business community, a total of eleven people.

Meeting Situation: The meeting started at 2:30 pm and adjourned at 4:15 pm. Chairman Chen Jian'an continued to discuss the issues that were not resolved at the last meeting. The representatives of the committee members present all expressed their opinions. After the meeting, the reporter of the Central News Agency learned through various inquiries that the meeting yesterday had not yet reached a consensus. The point of contention was still the silver content of the new currency. At the last meeting, some people advocated casting new coins in accordance with the currency system regulations of the third year of the Republic of China. Although the government would bear significant expenses, it seemed to be the government's obligation to seek permanent benefits and convenience for the people. However, another group believed that the government's burden of casting costs might be overwhelming under the current circumstances, so they advocated reducing the silver content. Because the above two opinions could not be reconciled, the first meeting did not produce a result, and it was agreed to continue the discussion yesterday. During the three-day recess, although various parties had consulted and communicated, the parties had not yet reached a consensus. Some Westerners also expressed their opinions, saying that since the government is determined, it should seek a thorough result. Although the government cannot raise the 30 million casting fees at once, it can cast in batches. The above-mentioned 30 million is the cost of casting all new coins, but in fact, it can be cast in batches. However, the silver content of the new currency must not be reduced again, otherwise all old coins must be melted and recast. In this case, the casting cost will be more than 30 million. If the fineness of the new and old coins is not uniform, not only will the purpose of reorganizing the currency system not be achieved, but there will still be trouble in foreign exchange and even greater impact on international trade. Since there were new opinions at the meeting, it was even more difficult to make a decision. Moreover, this meeting is for research purposes, soliciting unanimous opinions for the government to adopt. If a consensus cannot be reached, various opinions must be conveyed separately for selection. Since the two sides did not get closer, it was decided to continue the meeting at a later date. During this recess period, all parties are expected to continue to liaise.

Report to Song: Chen Jian'an, the chairman of the association, went to Song's residence on Qiqi Road at 5 pm yesterday to pay a visit to Finance Minister Song and report on the progress of the meeting that day. He left after talking for about 20 minutes. According to Chen's statement to the reporter, today (i.e., yesterday's meeting), because the opinions of the members and representatives were not yet unified, there was no resolution. It is now scheduled for next Wednesday (August 3) to hold the third meeting at the Central Bank to continue the discussion.

The First Batch of Postal Workers From the Northeast Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 162

Originally One Hundred and Three People This Month

Only Seven People Arrived Due to Japanese Searches

After the Japanese instigated rebels to seize postal rights in the three northeastern provinces, the Ministry of Communications announced the blockade of postal services in the Northeast and ordered postal workers in the area to leave their posts and enter the pass to report to nearby post offices in order to find ways to resettle them. Therefore, after receiving the order to blockade postal services in the Northeast, postal workers from various bureaus in the Northeast tried to change clothes and enter the pass. The first batch of postal workers entering the pass arrived in Shanghai on the Fengtian Maru at 5 pm yesterday. The details of their arrival in Shanghai are recorded as follows:

Welcoming Personnel: The Shanghai Postal Administration received a telegram from the Qingdao Postal Bureau yesterday morning reporting that the first batch of 103 postal workers from the Northeast would arrive in Shanghai on the Fengtian Maru on the afternoon of the 30th. Therefore, the bureau sent postman Wang A'gen with more than 30 postal workers and three trucks to the port on time to take care of the luggage of the postal workers arriving in Shanghai. Those who arrived at the port yesterday to welcome the postal workers included Shanghai Postmaster Zha Peilin, Deputy Postmaster Wu Yu, Inland Deputy Postmaster Wu Xi, Mail Postmaster Yan Nuo'an, Liaoning Deputy Postmaster Liu Yaoting, and Postal Workers' Union representatives Xu Duo and Lin Bingyu, about 40 people in total.

Postal Workers Arriving in Shanghai: Originally, there were 103 postal workers in the first batch coming to Shanghai. Because some were searched and detained by the Japanese army along the way, or had already reported to the post offices in Pingjin, only seven people, including family members, arrived in Shanghai yesterday. They include Gao Zongwen and his wife from the Liaoning District, Zhong Dating and his wife, Hua Cenhai, Zhang Hua and Li Xian from the Heilongjiang-Jilin District.

Entering the Pass: The reporter of the Central News Agency met with the postal workers who came to Shanghai yesterday and asked about their experience of entering the pass. According to Mr. Zhang and Mr. Li from the Heilongjiang-Jilin District, after the Harbin Post Office received the instruction from the Ministry of Communications to blockade postal services in the Northeast on the night of the 25th, the postal workers of various post offices packed their luggage that night and prepared to enter the pass the next day. At that time, four Japanese postal workers in the Harbin Post Office saw this and immediately notified the Japanese authorities. Before long, Japanese police were densely deployed around the post offices, prohibiting postal workers from leaving the bureau. The situation was unbearable. Therefore, the first to escape from the Heilongjiang-Jilin District, except for the two of us, are probably still trapped. As for our experience of entering the pass, we obtained the secret assistance of a secretary in the local American consulate. The two of us changed clothes and took a car to Changchun on the morning of the 26th, and then took the Fengtian Maru via Dalian to Shanghai. From Harbin to Changchun, the car was searched twice by the Japanese police. If there was a slight misunderstanding in the conversation, they would be detained. From Changchun to Dalian, we were interrogated three times on the ship. In short, within the scope of the Japanese army's power, all kinds of oppression cannot be described in words. As for the postal workers in the Heilongjiang-Jilin District who have not entered the pass, it is not known when they will be able to start their journey due to various environmental obstacles. According to Mr. Gao, a postal worker from the Liaoning District who came to Shanghai, the difficulties of entering the pass and the barbarity of the Japanese army have long been seen by Chinese and foreign people. It is undeniable that our colleagues were subjected to searches and humiliation by the Japanese side. Because there are thousands of postal workers in the Northeast who are eager to go south, I don't want to add more details to increase the danger for the postal workers left outside the pass when they enter the pass in the future. After the postal workers got off the ship, they shook hands with all the welcoming personnel one by one before taking the car to return to their private residences to rest.

Reporting to the Bureau: After the postal workers from the Northeast arrived in Shanghai, they originally intended to report to the general bureau immediately. However, because they arrived in Shanghai yesterday, it was past office hours, and today is Sunday, so they decided to report to the bureau tomorrow morning and pay a visit to Director-General Huang Naishu to report in person on the situation after the postal services in the Northeast were seized.

More to Come: After the arrival of the first batch, there will be more batches coming to Shanghai soon. It is also learned that some postal workers who have left their posts have been detained by the Japanese police, who have coerced and lured them to work as inspectors, specializing in inspecting postal workers entering the pass. A postal worker named Shen has been detained as many as three times and is still not out of danger.

The Appearance of Counterfeit Stamps: According to the postal workers from the Northeast who arrived in Shanghai, the counterfeit stamps issued by the rebels had already been printed and were scheduled to be sold on August 1. The appearance of the stamps featured pagodas or Puyi's image, and the colors varied. The denominations were one cent, two cents, five cents, and one dime.

Large Quantities of Japanese Goods Arrived 163

Transshipment Companies Refuse to Load

The Japanese Postal Company's Tsukuba Maru imported 16,745 pieces of Japanese goods, including several hundred pieces of American cotton and a batch of cement. The rest were all Japanese goods, mostly piece goods, but also a lot of groceries. The Mikasa Maru also transported more than 6,900 pieces. Yesterday, they were all unloaded at the two wharves of Huishan Post Ship. Some of the goods will be transshipped to Hankou by the Nisshin Maru.

In view of the large number of inferior goods, the transshipment companies along the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway convened a meeting of their peers and unanimously refused to load the goods for railway transport. They also notified all their peers not to be confused by the consignors' attempts to mix in goods when loading, and that each company should be responsible for paying attention to inspections to avoid mixed transport.

The Recent Activities of the 164

Blood Soul Anti-Treason Squad

Suppressing the Sale of Japanese Goods

Prohibiting the High Price of Domestic Products

Declaring No Fundraising

Warning to Chinese Stores: A Chinese store across from the Nanjing Road Continental Commercial Building received a warning letter from the "Shanghai Blood Soul Anti-Treason Squad" at 5 pm yesterday (the 30th), along with a bomb. The letter reads as follows: "Chinese Store, be informed, immediately stop selling all Japanese goods and publish a statement in the newspaper to show your sincerity. We are leaving a bomb as a warning. Shanghai Blood Soul Anti-Treason Squad, July 30."

Warning to the Brokers' Association: After the squad warned the yarn and cloth exchanges with bombs, almost no one asked about Japanese yarn and cloth. Some merchants, disregarding the overall situation, raised the price of domestic cotton yarn sharply, which affected the sales of domestic cotton yarn. The squad also sent a letter to the yarn and cloth exchange warning them. The letter reads as follows: "Our squad, in this time of national crisis, believes that every citizen has a duty to do their part, and therefore does not hesitate to sacrifice everything to strictly suppress treacherous merchants who buy and sell Japanese goods, in order to achieve the purpose of saving the country and the people. Unexpectedly, Zhang Yuchang, broker No. 27 of your exchange, and Xu Yongnian, broker No. 56, raised the price of domestic cotton yarn sharply at a time when Japanese goods were disappearing from the market due to the boycott. Such disregard for the overall situation and arbitrary monopoly has led merchants who only care about profit to regard domestic cotton yarn as a dangerous path and have to engage in the business of inferior goods. Their crime is no less than that of treacherous merchants who sell Japanese goods. They should be severely punished immediately. Considering that this is their first offense, we hereby issue a solemn warning. We hope that your exchange will forward this to all members for their information. In the future, do not raise the price of domestic products, otherwise the bullets are merciless, do not try lightly. To the Yarn and Cloth Exchange Brokers' Association, Shanghai Blood Soul Anti-Treason Squad, July 30."

Declaring No Fundraising: The squad's purpose is to eliminate treacherous merchants who sell Japanese goods. It does not raise funds from the outside world, fearing that unscrupulous elements will use the squad's name to extort money. It has specially engraved a seal and sent a letter to this newspaper declaring: "(Letter 1) Dear Sir, in order to prevent unscrupulous elements from borrowing our squad's name to engage in extortion or other illegal activities, we have specially engraved a seal with the text 'Shanghai Blood Soul Anti-Treason Squad', which will be used from July 30. Any document that does not bear our squad's seal in the future is a forgery. We hereby inform you and ask for your attention. To the Editorial Department of Shen Bao, Shanghai Blood Soul Anti-Treason Squad, July 30, attached seal one."

"(Letter 2) Dear Sir, our squad is purely organized by patriotic volunteers and has extremely strict discipline. Our only purpose is to eliminate treacherous merchants who sell Japanese goods. The squad's expenses are entirely raised by the comrades in the squad and we do not raise funds from the outside world. In the future, we will not be responsible for any fundraising or fraud in the name of our squad. Please pay attention to this. Yesterday's Press Visit 165

To the War Zone's Epidemic Prevention Work

The War Zone's Sanitary Facilities Are Still Good

Significant Results in Preventing Cholera

The Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the Shanghai-Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Committee, jointly organized by the Health Department and the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, has achieved remarkable results in handling health and epidemic prevention matters in the war zone since its establishment. During this hot summer, severe epidemics are prevalent, especially in the war zone. Because of the effective epidemic prevention, as of yesterday, 161 cases of true cholera had been discovered in Songhu, Baojia, Taikun, etc., with 94 deaths. Yesterday, the Health Bureau and the Epidemic Prevention Group of the Rehabilitation Committee specially invited the press to visit the health and epidemic prevention work in the war zones of Songhu, Jiabao, and others. They departed from the Health Bureau at 10 am yesterday morning and returned in the evening. The details are recorded as follows:

Liu Ruiheng's Speech: More than 30 reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers gathered at the Health Bureau at 9:30 am yesterday morning. Director Hu Hongji introduced Health Minister Liu Ruiheng, who gave a speech, saying: "Unfortunately, the country is suffering from frequent disasters, including internal strife, red bandits, floods, national wars, and epidemics, to name a few. Cholera is especially rampant, from Nanchang and Baiyue to Pingjin in the north, and from the coast to Yichang in the Yangtze River Basin, and the provinces of Shaanxi, Shanxi, and Suiyuan in the northwest. There are many deaths, so we should pay close attention to prevention. The Health and Epidemic Prevention Group of the Shanghai-Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Committee, which I am in charge of as director and Director Hu Hongji as deputy director for Shanghai and Jin Baoshan as deputy director for the four counties of Baojia, Taikun, has been engaged in epidemic prevention work for six weeks. As of yesterday, only 161 cases of true cholera had been discovered in the four counties of the inland combat zone, which can be said to be a result of serious prevention. Epidemic prevention work includes preventive injections, well water disinfection, and epidemic prevention propaganda, etc. Analyzing cholera, it is truly a disease that enters through the mouth. Therefore, even if we do our best to give injections and disinfect, if we do not make the lower-level people understand the importance of cleanliness in their diet, we will still not be effective. Therefore, among the three, propaganda is the most important. I would like to express my gratitude for the energetic propaganda given by the press in the past. In the future, please continue to pay attention to arousing the lower-level people to pay attention to cleanliness and resist disasters together. Please visit various places to see that the epidemic prevention work is not lax."

The Mobile Clinic on Hengfeng Road (Photo by Li Zunyong) 166

After Mr. Liu Ruiheng's report on the tour's itinerary was completed, the tour commenced at 10:15 AM, with the following schedule: Depart from the Nanshi Health Bureau at 10:00 AM; inspect the mobile clinic at 3 Hengfeng Road at 10:30 AM; observe the inoculation site at the Shanghai-Taiyuan Long-Distance Bus Station at 10:45 AM; at 11:15 AM, observe the water disinfection efforts by the Boy Scouts in Dachang; proceed to the inoculation team in Luodian at 12:00 PM; visit the Jia Ding Plague Hospital at 12:45 PM; have lunch and rest at Kuishan Park in Jia Ding from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM; proceed to the Baoshan Plague Hospital at 3:30 PM, where they would be received by Mr. Wang Qingtao, the District Chief of Baoshan First District, who would show them around the area; observe the Wusong mobile clinic at 4:00 PM; observe the disinfection of the river at Baziqiao at 5:00 PM; and at 6:00 PM, visit the Health Bureau's Health Laboratory (189 Guangdong Street, Qiujiang Road) to observe their various projects and watch a health-related film.

A Glimpse of the War Zone: The areas visited yesterday included Zhabei, Baoshan, Jia Ding, and Wusong. Zhabei remained a scene of ruins and devastation, with remnants of the past still visible. The recently recovered areas, such as Liuying Road, Yokohama Road, and Tongji Road, had not yet been restored and were sparsely populated. Only small groups of two or three scavenging children were occasionally seen passing by. Baoshan also suffered significant losses, mostly indirectly. Since its recovery, major efforts have been made to reorganize the area, but the damaged buildings have not been restored due to financial constraints. The population has also decreased by 30-40%. The area outside the East Gate of Jia Ding suffered the most from looting, while remnants of wartime activity could still be seen on Dongda Street in the city. Kuishan Park had been used as a garrison by the Japanese troops, who caused damage before their departure, a destruction of beauty that was deeply regrettable. The other areas suffered only minor damage. Only Yuncaobang in Wusong was relatively bustling, while the town itself remained a field of rubble. Residents who had lost their homes had built makeshift grass huts in Yuncaobang to provide themselves with shelter, a truly pitiful sight.

The Epidemic Prevention Situation: When the reporters first arrived at the mobile clinic on 3 Hengfeng Road, they found one doctor and three female nurses, who were administering free vaccinations against epidemics. On average, they could vaccinate one hundred people per day. They then proceeded to Dachang, where they found the No. 1 Team of the 65th Regiment of the Boy Scout Firefighting Corps, consisting of nine members, working in Baoshan. The No. 1 and No. 5 Districts had already been completed, and they were now working on the No. 3 District. They then proceeded to Luodian, where the people were resistant to vaccination due to their ignorance. The inoculation team had to patiently persuade them before they would agree. The Jia Ding Plague Hospital was better equipped, with three or four doctors and nurses. It had opened on the 2nd of this month and had already admitted fifty plague victims. More than thirty had recovered, and six had died (two of the six were already dying when they were brought to the hospital, and three were addicted to opium and therefore difficult to treat). After lunch, they went to the Baoshan Plague Hospital, which had similar equipment to the Jia Ding Hospital, but was scheduled to open the following day. They then inspected the Shanghai-Wusong war zone and visited the Zhabei Health Laboratory (where they were guided through the various health laboratories by Director Cheng Shuzhen and shown health films and films about the lab's production of smallpox vaccine (the lab's vaccine is available for sale).

The tour ended at 6:00 PM. Overall, the health work in the various districts was quite complete, but the areas were vast and the number of staff was small, so it was feared that it would be difficult to cover the entire area.

The Japanese Consulate Prepares to Negotiate with Us

Cotton Cloth Guild 169

Held General Membership Meeting Yesterday

Re-elected Seven Executive Committee Members and Added Seven Supervisory Committee Members

Resolved to Severely Sanction Fellow Traders Who Privately Smuggle Enemy Goods

The Shanghai Cotton Cloth Trade Association held a general membership meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, with more than 200 members in attendance. Chairman Chen Songshen and Ke Ganchen presided over the meeting. The chairman gave a report, followed by the re-election of the executive and supervisory committee members, and the resolution of several important cases. The details are recorded below.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Chen Songyuan reported that today is the third general membership meeting of the association. He felt deeply honored and grateful that representatives from higher authorities and members had come despite the sweltering heat. He noted that the association had been reorganized on August 15th of the 19th year of the Republic (1930) and had now been in existence for two years. He was deeply grateful to the industry for not abandoning him and entrusting him with the position of chairman, but he feared that he was not capable of handling the heavy responsibilities. Furthermore, his other responsibilities prevented him from concentrating on association affairs, which made him feel even more ashamed. Therefore, since taking office, he had been conscientious and careful, seeking only to avoid mistakes and not seeking credit, so as not to disappoint the industry's trust. Now that the re-election was imminent, he hoped that everyone would elect someone more capable so that he could be relieved of his responsibilities and reduce his mistakes. This was his sincere request. The report on the handled affairs of the previous year had already been printed and distributed to the members, and he had already received their understanding, so he would not repeat them. As for the affairs of this year, he would report them to everyone and ask for their guidance. However, since the weather today was very hot and there was still the re-election and discussion of various proposals to be held, in order to save time and avoid having everyone sit in the heat for too long, he would select the most important items to present to everyone. The remaining items would still be compiled into a report and distributed to the members for their review. He noted that the most important tasks handled this year were five: (1) resistance to enemy goods; (2) fundraising for disaster relief; (3) collection of business tax on behalf of the government; (4) special establishment of a temporary interest-free loan office and allocation of funds to relieve compatriots in distress; (5) comforting the 19th Route Army. (The original report was very long and is omitted.)

Elected Executive and Supervisory Committee Members: The results of the election of the Executive Committee members were: Zhang Maorong received votes, Xia Xianting received 89 votes, Shi Yunmao received 87 votes, Fu Zhenyuan received 52 votes, Pan Yushu received 48 votes, Zhou Weishi received 41 votes, and Bu Bo received 34 votes. The alternate executive committee members were: Gao Jiyun received 34 votes, Zhu Mingqiu received 33 votes, Sun Xiaozhu received 29 votes, Li Shuiru received 24 votes, Ma Yinsun received 22 votes, Wang Jinru received 16 votes, and Huang Liyao received 14 votes. The supervisory committee members were: Ke Ganchen received 111 votes, Li Xuechang received 93 votes, Li Shaoqing received 72 votes, Gu Ziquan received 50 votes, Zhou Rongsun received 73 votes, Xu Xueming received 69 votes, and Qin Lansun received 69 votes. The alternate supervisory committee members were: Li Zhonghui received 22 votes, Yao Shanfu received 11 votes, and Deng Zhonghe received 7 votes.

Resolutions: The resolutions were as follows: (1) The final account for the 20th year of the Republic (1931) was approved. (2) The budget for the 21st year of the Republic (1932) was approved. (3) The proposal from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to organize a national crisis reserve fund was approved in principle. The specific measures were to be drafted by the Executive Committee, taking into account the specific circumstances of the industry, and then implemented. (4) A proposal to severely sanction the private smuggling of enemy goods and issue a statement to the outside world was approved. If any member was found to be privately smuggling enemy goods, after verification, they would be expelled from the association according to the rules, and a public announcement would be made in the newspaper for public judgment. The external statement was approved for publication.

Sanctioning Treacherous Merchants and Severely Sanctioning the Private Smuggling of Enemy Goods: After the Wan Xian Massacre occurred, the association convened a general meeting and resolved to establish an Economic Sanctions Against Japan Committee to be responsible for handling matters related to resisting enemy goods. When the Pan case occurred, they intensified their efforts, expanded their organization, reorganized the Economic Sanctions Against Japan Committee into the Cotton Cloth Industry Anti-Japanese Committee, and established inspection and investigation departments to cut off trade with Japanese merchants and strictly inspect smuggling. As a result, enemy goods disappeared from the market. In the past, the achievements of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce have been praised in letters. This was all due to the enthusiasm of the entire industry, the efforts of the staff, and the dedication of the staff. They hoped to maintain this momentum and use it to put Japanese merchants to death. However, overnight, various anti-Japanese organizations were disbanded by explicit order due to unreasonable demands, and the anti-Japanese affairs of the industry were also effectively suspended. However, the association, in view of the great suffering of the people during the Shanghai War, deeply felt that the only way to seek self-preservation was to resist enemy goods, so it continued to persevere in its original purpose. On March 9th, May 3rd, and May 16th, it repeatedly sent letters to its members with earnest advice and employed specialists to secretly investigate the sealing of old goods and formulate measures for their disposal. In addition to requesting the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to adopt them in order to circulate finance and preserve the capital of merchants, they printed "Volunteer Statements Not to Sell Japanese Goods" and distributed them to fellow traders to fill out in order to show their good faith and bind them. Everything within their powers was done to the best of their ability. However, due to the lure of great profits, many people rushed to smuggle enemy goods as their numbers grew. Only one-third of members joined the association, which made it difficult to popularize power and was hindered by lack of support. In order to resolve this, we are submitting it to the general assembly for resolution and severe sanction to be followed and to consolidate the front line of resistance.

Emergency Statement from the Cotton Cloth Trade Association: An urgent statement: Since the January 28th Incident, the association has repeatedly received letters and packages delivered by post, some signed as a part of the industry, the Sulphur Bomb Group, Feng Shengli, Wenye Gongqi, the Special Inspection Department of the National Salvation Corps, a member of the cotton cloth industry, an industry member, Bei Lifei Xiang Zhengqing, and the Blood Soul Elimination Group, as well as a letter left behind, attached with a tin of biscuits, with a handmade grenade inside. Upon reviewing the meaning of the letters, they all warned traders not to sell smuggled enemy goods again. All of the letters received by the association did not have addresses, so there was no way to reply. In addition to publishing the original letters separately in the market so that traders could be aware of them, we also sent a letter to the police station to take away the grenades to avoid danger. We also stated that the matter concerned the patriotic movement and we did not wish to investigate it deeply. Everything that was done was out of patriotic zeal, and who among those with blood and Qi would not deeply sympathize? However, the association is in this environment, and the difficulties of handling the process and measures are something that outsiders cannot fully understand. Here is a brief summary of the points: (1) The handling process. After the Wan Xian Massacre occurred, the association immediately convened a general meeting of members and resolved to organize a specialized committee for economic severance to be responsible for handling matters related to resisting enemy goods, and sent a letter to all members immediately stopping the purchase of enemy goods. As the Shen incident continued, the association strengthened its work, expanded its organization, added inspection and investigation groups, implemented inspection seals, strictly prevented smuggling, and enemy goods disappeared from the market. The Chamber of Commerce sent a letter expressing appreciation. Afterwards, the anti-Japanese groups suddenly received an explicit order to dissolve, and the Jiaodaoji lost their strength greatly, however, in light of the horrors suffered by the people during the Shanghai war, and feeling that the only way to seek self-preservation was to come, the association repeatedly sent letters to members, urging them to take the overall situation into consideration and adhere to the bottom line and never be willing to be included in the ranks of treacherous merchants, and printed a vow not to sell enemy goods voluntary letter, which was sent to members to fill in to prevent duels and reveal credibility, while employing experts to secretly conduct investigations, and those who did not follow dissuasion were warned with strict letters, and if they still did not know how to repent, the final punishment was given to them. Wherever power can reach, we do our best.

(2) The difficulties of measures. The association is a trading group, so from its own position, it takes the members' wishes as its wishes, and the members' interests should be absolutely guaranteed. And the power is regulated by law, the way things are done should be put on the right track, can only be dissuaded and cannot be forced, if I go my own way, I will be in violation of the law and overstepping my powers, and the members who have joined the association only account for 25% of the total members of the association, so it is difficult to popularize the power and lack of support. In general, if things can be united and consistent, then no matter what difficulties are encountered, they will eventually be solved smoothly, otherwise, they will take care of this and lose that, and the person in charge will be exhausted and unable to help. However, the association loves the country and will never lag behind, and no matter what, we will still pursue our original intention, continue to work hard, do our best, seek peace of mind, and never change our minds. If we are blessed with Jia Mou from all walks of life, we will accept it as much as possible. This is a solemn statement, and we hope that you will be kind and clear.

Local News Two

China Merchants Electric Company 170

Zhu Shaoyi's Lawsuit

The Local Court Opened the Trial Yesterday

Zhu Shuyi's Previous Grudges

Fu Chongde Suddenly Suffers from Heatstroke

Lu Ji Yun Claims to Know Nothing

Zhu Shaoyi, the director of the transportation department of the China Merchants Electric Company, was sued because the dismissal of ticket seller No. 71 was opposed by the Trade Union of Water and Electricity Workers, triggering a strike. Leaflets and slogans were posted with various abusive words against Zhu Shaoyi, Zhu Zi, and Zhu Zhizai. Later, Zhu Shaoyi claimed that the slogans and leaflets did not represent the views of all the workers, but were advocated by Lu Jiyun of No. 3 and Che Chuan Chongde of No. 7. He then hired a lawyer to sue in the local court. After the prosecutor released Lu and Fu on bail, a public prosecution was filed, and the criminal court scheduled a trial for yesterday. The trial began at 12:00 noon yesterday in the third court presided over by Judge Huang Changyuan. Many workers were in attendance. Zhu Shaoyi testified that he was 55 years old, from Shanghai, residing at 135 Shengyi Lane, and the transportation director of the China Merchants Electric Company. He was suing Lu Jiyun and Fu Chongde for defamation, harming his reputation, and plotting against him. The methods of harm included issuing leaflets, posting slogans, placing excrement in cigarette cases in front of the company gate, and gathering people to guard the gate, all with the intention of plotting against and insulting him. He claimed that they were directed by these two people. Furthermore, his son was a staff member in the general affairs department and engineering division, and his duties were separate from his own. However, they compared his son and him to dogs in their propaganda and made up facts such as bribery. The judge asked who issued the leaflets. He replied that it was the drivers and ticket sellers, but the masterminds were the two of them. The judge asked how he knew. He replied that there were witnesses. The judge asked when this happened. He replied that on May 29th, they held a meeting at the Ningbo Hotel in the French Concession, and on June 1st, they issued leaflets, posted slogans, and attempted to harm him with filth. Therefore, he was afraid of danger and did not go to the company. On June 2nd, someone reported that Lu Jiyun was spreading rumors on the bus, saying bad things about him. When the passengers asked him why he wrote "all workers," Lu pointed to his chest and said that he was responsible and would not only defeat him but also treat him to snacks. Witness Ding Baoshan could testify. The judge asked if there was a union in his company. He replied that there was, and it was for workers, not for staff. However, inspectors represented the transportation director externally and were also staff members. In the past, they joined the union, and the company had no power to stop them. There were 700 people in the union, but only 300 in the transportation department. He had evidence, including a "Current Affairs News" newspaper, a declaration, a slogan, an urgent notice, and a "New News" tabloid. They were calling meetings, such as "drivers who don't drive will have their hats taken away" and "ticket sellers who don't sell tickets will have their ticket boxes taken away." He was one of the founders of the company and a shareholder, and everything was done according to the regulations, which inevitably made some people unhappy. As for Lu Jiyun, he was originally ticket seller No. 27 and was repeatedly promoted from ticket checker to scheduler and then to inspector. Later, when a staff position opened up in the transportation department, he submitted the names of three inspectors to General Manager Lu Bohong, but in the end, inspector No. 2 was promoted, and Lu resented him for not helping him. However, he only had the power to submit the names; he did not know anything else. Regarding Fu Chongde, he was originally a ticket seller from No. 41 and was promoted to scheduler. He was once a standing member of the union and had disputes when he represented the company at labor-management disputes. Later, Fu was arrested on suspicion of being a communist and blamed him for not protecting him, but he had no power to do so. Regarding ticket sellers Nos. 116 and 71, they were reported by ticket checkers for fraud. After review, it was reported to the General Manager, and then the director of the lighting department, Lu Zhonglin, was assigned to reinvestigate. Then the General Manager decided to dismiss the two, and some people took the opportunity to make trouble for him. However, on June 1st, the standing committee of the union made a statement to the manager and did not advocate for it. Later, they surrounded the directors' office, and ticket seller No. 71 was reinstated. He had been in business for 40 years and had never seen this kind of phenomenon.

The judge asked about the witnesses. He replied that they were Liu Fusheng, Ding Baoshan, Ling Jitan, Chief Liu, Lu Bohong, and Feng Liutang. The judge said that Feng had issued a statement saying that he knew nothing. He replied that they accused him of ten crimes, and Feng Liutang was still the interrogator.

Since there was no such fact at all, the matter was dropped. At that time, Feng was even more dignified than a judge, how could he come to write a letter claiming to know nothing? Because the company could not guarantee his safety, he sought legal remedy, and a group of workers published in the newspaper that they did not recognize them and immediately hit them. At this point, Fu Chongde suffered from heatstroke and returned home, while Lu Jiyun said that he was 37 years old, from Shanghai, and lived at 20 Longhua Road. He knew nothing about the union's disputes with Mr. Zhu and had no idea why he was being sued. Therefore, he answered "I don't know" to the judge's questions. The judge then ordered that

witnesses be summoned for another hearing.

Failure of French Silk Merchants 171

Impacts Chinese Silk Merchants

Yi Da Company Unable to Repay Debts

Banque de l'Indochine and British Bank File a Joint Lawsuit

Wu Yuntai, the owner of Yongda Silk Shop at 38 Avenue Edward VII, Tang Yeqin, the accountant of Jiucheng Silk Factory at 4 Xinkang Road, and Wu Shenbo are all well-known silk merchants in the city. They had previously pooled their capital to form Yi Da Co., Ltd., which specialized in exporting raw silk, mostly to France for sale. At the end of 1929, Dufour, a famous French silk merchant, went out of business and suddenly went bankrupt. The French silk market was greatly affected, and silk prices plummeted. The silk shipped to France by Yi Da Company was all accepted and discounted by Banque de l'Indochine. With Dufour's bankruptcy, the drafts could not be honored and became worthless paper.

The debt owed to Banque de l'Indochine, as of April 17th of last year, after deducting the deposit and other funds, still amounted to 137,966 francs, equivalent to 25,155.641 silver dollars. Yi Da was repeatedly urged to repay the debt, but Wu Yuntai and others all shirked responsibility, claiming that they were only directors of the company and were not responsible for the company's debt. Therefore, the debt had not yet been repaid. Banque de l'Indochine recently hired lawyers Yang Linzhi, Zhang Jiahui, Ye Shaoying, and Chen Zhongyin to file a lawsuit against Wu and the other two, detailing the reasons why the defendants should be liable for Yi Da's debt, stating that whether the company was legally established at the time the contract in this case occurred was still to be proven, and even if it was legally established, Yi Da had invested all of its capital in silk purchased on behalf of Dufour at the end of 1929. Once Dufour went bankrupt, the remittance naturally could not be honored, and the defendants were well aware that the price of French silk had also plummeted at the same time. The defendants could not devise a good plan for the company's business, and they did not convene a shareholders' meeting to declare liquidation or file for bankruptcy at this time. What else were they waiting for? According to the above explanation, the defendants had violated Article 161 of the company regulations, the duties that directors should fulfill. According to the interpretation of the Judicial Yuan No. 92 in the 18th year of the Judicial Yuan (1929), they should be responsible to the creditors. Therefore, they requested that the court immediately summon the defendants for trial and order them to be jointly and severally liable for the repayment. In addition to being sued by Banque de l'Indochine, British Bank has also recently filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court to recover debts. The subject of the lawsuit is exactly the same, so the two plaintiffs jointly requested the court to combine the two cases for trial to facilitate matters. Yesterday, Judge Shen Hong specially opened the 10th court to summon the two sides for final oral arguments and ordered them to leave and await the verdict.

Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of the Chinese district, yesterday instructed Wen Yingxing, the director of the Public Security Bureau, to order a special curfew in the areas under his jurisdiction from 12:00 tonight until 10:00 PM the following day (i.e., the 1st) to prevent rioters from causing trouble. At the same time, the Municipal Council's security vehicles will be patrolling the roads fully loaded with armed detectives to prevent trouble. The French Concession authorities have also ordered all detectives to be fully armed and dispatched tomorrow morning to intensify prevention measures. Kong Xiangxi Suffering from Influenza 177

Planned Departure Abroad Likely to be Postponed Again

The Guowen News Agency reports that Kong Xiangxi, the special envoy investigating industries in various countries, had accumulated fatigue during his previous trips between Pingjin and Jinghan during the hot summer. After returning to Shanghai, he suffered from influenza due to frequent social engagements and preparing for his journey, coupled with the unfavorable season. As a result, he was unable to depart as scheduled. A reporter visited his private residence yesterday to inquire about his condition. According to his doctor, Kong contracted influenza on the 25th. The initial condition was quite severe, with his body temperature rising to 104 degrees Fahrenheit. After treatment, it has gradually decreased. However, after the fever subsided, he felt weak, so he needs to rest for another week to recover. Therefore, Kong's departure abroad is likely to be postponed until mid-August.

Taxpayers' Association 184

Protesting the Change of Collection of Taxes to Silver

Letter Sent to the Public Works Department Yesterday

The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the General Office of the Public Works Department of the Shanghai International Settlement yesterday, which reads: To whom it may concern, According to a letter from the Shanghai Baohua Shoe and Hat Store, our store sent a letter to your association on the 9th of this month regarding the Public Works Department's change of collecting police donations in silver, requesting you to write a letter to negotiate the matter, and also sent a letter to the Public Works Department on the same day, urging them to correct the matter. On the 11th, we received a reply from your association, informing us that negotiations had been made, which we deeply appreciate. However, on the 18th, we received a reply from the Public Works Department, stating that they received our letter of July 9, questioning the bureau's changing the method of collecting donations without cause. In fact, the bureau is still collecting according to the usual practice and has not changed. Because the house where your store resides is of Western style, it must be valued in silver. The estimated price is 288 taels of silver per month, and the quarterly donation should be 120 taels, 9 mace, and 6 fen of silver. The foreign exchange rate is calculated at 7 mace and 2 fen. To avoid cumbersome procedures, 7 mace and 2 fen is set as the permanent standard. When collecting donations, it is calculated according to the market price of the day. If the foreign exchange rate falls and your store does not want to suffer losses, you can pay with regular silver. This kind of reply is completely contradictory and cannot convince people. Our store's rent is paid in silver dollars (400 yuan per month), and it should be calculated in silver dollars. However, the bureau abandons the simple and uses silver to pay the donation, and when pricing, it uses 7 mace and 2 fen as the permanent standard, but when collecting donations, it uses the recent market price (6 mace and 9 fen) as a temporary change. Even if we take a step back and recognize this contradictory method as the authority of the bureau, last year the foreign exchange rate was often above 7 mace and 2 fen, and the highest price was close to 7 mace and 3 fen. If the donation paid by our store was calculated at the market price of the day, the amount should be within 168 yuan, but why did the bureau collect 168 silver dollars per quarter without calculating according to the market price of the day or mentioning that regular silver of 120 taels, 9 mace, and 6 fen could be used to pay the donation? If this is the case, taxpayers only have to bear an extra loss of 168 yuan, without enjoying the benefit of 168 yuan, which is very unfair. We have attached a copy of the rent bill and the bureau's reply for your reference. After investigating the arguments of the store, we found that they were very reasonable and sufficient, while the reasons held by your bureau could not justify themselves. Because it is not based on fairness, it is difficult to convince people. The sharp fall in the foreign exchange rate means that your bureau's expenditures are mostly in silver, and the losses suffered are not small, but merchants and residents also cannot be exceptions. Moreover, when the foreign exchange rate was high, your bureau benefited from collecting silver dollars. Managing public undertakings should ultimately be simple. Going from simplicity to complexity, seeking petty profits, and harming others to benefit oneself is most inappropriate. Recently, the movement to abolish taels and use yuan is precisely to prevent this kind of currency instability, which often causes changes in people's income and expenditure. It is unbelievable that your bureau's wisdom has not seen this. However, in order to make up for the losses, your bureau has adopted this kind of inconsistent policy, which is understandable, but the matter is ultimately unfair. It is ultimately difficult to accept being convenient to oneself as the primary principle. Fortunately, the rent is calculated in silver dollars, so collecting the commonly circulated silver dollars is also convenient and simple. Why bother with repeated calculations, which lead to many disturbances? If your bureau's budget is indeed insufficient, there are ways to balance it. Increasing revenue and reducing expenditure are originally permitted by the facts. If you want to increase income and do it piecemeal, or even make each taxpayer's prosperity decline day by day, then the number of sufferers in society will gradually increase, and there will be more problems with public security. It is feared that the funds collected will not be enough to compensate for the increasing costs of maintaining public security. This association is not arguing for the sake of argument, but because of its deep love for public prosperity, it has to speak out earnestly. According to the above letter, we hereby request your bureau to calculate the Shanghai Baohua Shoe Store's municipal donation based on the rent of 400 silver dollars, and continue to collect 168 silver dollars per quarter.

Six Grain and Rice Organizations 185

Preparing to Commemorate Ye Zhuanjun

August 13 at the Miscellaneous Grain Guild

The Shanghai Soybean and Rice Trade Association, the Jiangsu Provincial Rice Industry Federation in Shanghai, the Miscellaneous Grain, Oil Cake Trade Association, the Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Exchange, the Rice Shop Trade Association, and the Rice Milling Trade Association jointly organized a memorial service for Mr. Ye Huijun. Yesterday, a preparatory meeting was held on the third floor of the Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Guild. Since the soybean and rice industry guilds and the miscellaneous grain guild jointly elected Mr. Ye Huijun as chairman, and the government planned to establish a rice and grain inspection office that would collect 20 cents per stone, this matter was related to the people's livelihood. When our colleagues learned of this, they were extremely anxious and publicly requested Mr. Ye to go to Nanjing to petition the government and meet with Commander-in-Chief Chiang to explain all the difficulties and ask the government to withdraw the order. Commander-in-Chief Chiang sympathized with the difficulties of the merchants and agreed to do so, and the order was immediately cancelled. Mr. Ye devoted himself to the association's affairs and made great contributions to the industry. Now, due to his death from abdominal tumor, all of our colleagues deeply mourn him. At the meeting, the colleagues elected Gu Xinyi, Chen Ziyi, Cai Yukun, Fu Qiangeng, Jiang Zisheng, Zhu Zixiang, Yan Biquan, Jiang Hongbin, Chen Wenshao, She Bingwen, and others as members of the preparatory committee, and mutually elected Gu Xinyi as the director of the preparatory committee to handle the preparations. The venue for the memorial service was tentatively set at the Miscellaneous Grain Guild. It was decided that the memorial service would be held on August 13. The industry and the guild market would be closed for one day, and there would be a grand event at that time.

Dapeng Bay Pirates 186

Plotting to Rob Ships off the Coast of Taizhou - Police Warning

Public Works Department Notifies All Shipping Bureaus

Shanghai Shipping Companies to Take Strict Precautions

After the Taikoo Suiyang wheel was hijacked by Dapeng Bay pirates, the British Navy stationed in Hong Kong sent a warship to the area and bombarded dozens of villages with cannons. Many civilians were killed, and the bandits were forced to retreat slightly and find other ways out. They secretly went to the waters off Taizhou, Zhejiang, hoping to hijack ships. This city received a warning yesterday and has telegraphed all ships to take strict precautions. The situation is described in detail below:

Secretly Heading to Zhejiang Waters The Dapeng Bay pirates have a large-scale organization. Major ports in Shanghai, Hankou, Hong Kong, and Tianjin have established informant networks to scout out merchant ships carrying large sums of cash, and then they plan to rob them. After their old nest was bombed by British warships, the bandits dispersed in all directions. Recently, they gathered again. However, given that Chinese and British warships are often stationed in the South China Sea for escort, making it impossible to rob ships, they managed to leave Dapeng Bay and head to the waters off Taizhou, Zhejiang.

Shanghai Receives Report On the 29th (Friday), the Shanghai Public Works Department received an urgent secret telegram from Hong Kong, which stated that the Dapeng Bay pirates had secretly left the area and were heading to places such as Taizhou Island and Sandu Bay in Zhejiang, hoping to hijack merchant ships. Please inform the shipping bureaus operating on that route as soon as possible to take precautions to avoid accidents.

Shipping Industry Takes Strict Precautions After receiving the Public Works Department's secret report yesterday, all Chinese and foreign shipping companies in this city immediately notified the ships on the Nanyang route to take extra precautions when passing through the waters of Zhejiang and Taizhou Island. The ships on the Shanghai-Taiwan route paid even more attention after receiving the report. They were very careful when passengers boarded the ships, and the onboard police were also on special alert. The ships en route were also notified by telegram. At the same time, the Shanghai Naval Headquarters was notified to use wireless telegraphs to inform the warships to patrol Sandu Bay and Taizhou Island to protect shipping merchants.
